I'm getting Wheels on Meals here in Arroyo Seco while this craziness is going on and I understand that the food comes from Lawrence's and it's good stuff by anybody's standards. I've had chili relleno, meat loaf, BBQ beef on a french roll, to name a few, and today was shrimp and fries. The shrimp were so big when I first looked, I thought it was chicken. All meals come with green or potato salad and condiments. I've never been to King City but when we're done with the virus I plan on taking a trip to Lawrence's since I already know I won't be disappointed. BTW, thanks for what you do for the community. Frankly, five stars ain't enough!!!!<//Review>

No longer Lawrence's! Sadly another covid victim.  New owners, stopped in for breakfast, not good. I hope they get it together.  Be prepared for super long wait, we were only ones there for breakfast, restaurant empty. We had to ask for every single thing twice, took over an hour. Bread tasted of refrigerator, eggs over done and had a hint of last nights whatever chili from grill, bacon deep fried to death.  No water in restroom toilets, apparently they have sewage issues like full septic?  They need a cook that is experienced, waitresses who have done more than just eat in a restaurant, some decor vs. the prison look, advertising and all this will require a lot of cash they most likely do not have. Very sad.   The old kieffer's used to be so good, a go to way point in travel - long gone.  They might have great dinners, it appears the dinner menu looks like an extensive collection of Mexican food, but breakfast, the simplest meal was a big miss.<//Review>

<date>1563937189520<//date><rate>5<//rate>< Text>
This restaurant has been here since the 80s and my family and I used to come here about 10 years ago. I have since moved out of state and I just had to visit on my last trip to California this week. I am so glad I did. The quality is the same! Amazingly fresh fish. Do not come here if you are looking for the "Americanized" Sushi. This is traditional raw fish on rice, known as Nigiri. Don't skimp and order the Aki Special (who is the owner and head sushi chef). The Aki Special is his take on the "dynamite" and way better! Baby shrimp, scallops, crab, and mushrooms baked in Japanese mayo! You're missing out every time you go to another restaurant and not here.

Pictured: Salmon Nigiri, Baked Mussels, Aki Special, and the complementary ice cream at the end to help cleanse your palate. Not Pictured: the Nigiri I ate before taking a picture LOL.</Text>

Very nice place that isn't the hustle and bustle of other sushi places. If you are looking for hip this isn't it. If you are looking for good sushi in a relaxed environment this is it. They are also Dodger fans so the TV has them on when they are playing. Try the soft boned chicken and the miso mackerel on the appetizer menu.<//Review>

< review>
I was in the area for an event and wanted a quick dinner at Hakata Ramen, but I'd found that I'd gotten there too early and Hakata wouldn't be open for another 30 minutes! This place was right next door and I noticed they were open--problem solved. It's a small, neat and clean but unassuming-looking place, but I soon found out that I had wandered into a little gem. I was the first one there for the night and sat at the sushi bar. The chef, Aki, is kind of reserved, but he's a wiz with a sushi knife. I just started ordering everything that sounded good: Scallop, salmon, yellowtail (best), uni, spicy tuna handroll, ikura sushi, and finally the "Aki special"--basically a seafood dynamite that was very tasty. There's something so magical about baked Japanese mayo mixed with masago (smelt egg), yum. The fish was fresh and the portions generous. They even gave me a complimentary sorbet at the end--it was orange creamsicle-like and delicious! There was just one waitress working there at the time but she was very nice and efficient, no complaints at all with the service either. Sometimes when things don't go as planned you end up discovering something great! I will definitely return.< /review>

<review>Salmon nigiri- loved it! fatty, fresh, and melts in your mouth.
Octopus nigiri- yuck! Way chewy!
Yellowtail nigiri- mediocre
Dodger Roll- too much sauce that it overpowered the albacore. Rice didn't stick together and was falling as I picked up the sushi.
Spicy Tuna roll- meh. Not fresh at all and pretty bland.
Crispy chicken karage- no flavor. Just deep fried bits of chicken pieces.

All this for almost 50 bucks with tips included.
Probably won't be back anytime. Next time I crave for sushi I'll just drive to West LA or J-town.
BTW, this place is tiny! There's only 1 big table that sits a party of maybe 5? Definitely not good for big groups.< /review>< gmapID>

<review>One of the rare exceptions of fusion foods executed really well. Look beyond the novelty and you‚Äôll be graced with good eats.

I‚Äôve had the Ninja Cali Burrito, Ninja Fries, D-Bowl, Ninja Chicken Tacos, and even the Death Taco here, but I‚Äôll save the details on that monstrosity for the other location‚Äôs review page. If I remember right, Genkiyaki‚Äôs media state that they use a teriyaki sauce. I‚Äôve either been betrayed too often by inauthentic teriyaki sauce, or this isn‚Äôt teriyaki sauce at all. It‚Äôs not particularly soy sauce heavy and rather sweet and spicy in the literal sense, not the popcorn chicken dipping sauce sense. It reminds me a bit of galbi/kalbi marinade! The fries are seasoned almost like spicy BBQ chips, and are still even tossed in this seasoning rub while being laced with other sauces and toppings for the Ninja Fries. The bowl had a large portion of meat to rice amazingly. There was no skimping around here on any of the items! The tacos are a bit pricey though and not fantastic. Get tacos at more authentic joint, unless you‚Äôre jumping on the challenge. The only knock I can think of is that the flavour profile is very similar across the menu items, and the main difference between them is the choice of carb delivery. I think I prefer the burrito best. Also, there is a bit of heat in each item so if you‚Äôre not used to eating spice at all, expect just under sriracha levels of spice.

Friendly, quick service! The interior is basic and modern, with a wall showcasing the death taco challengers. It reminds me a bit of a coffee shop and there‚Äôs plenty of seating around for a group. You might get to spectate someone taking on the challenge as well and get to see if you want in on the action!

Definitely must try this joint. I wish it were closer to me so I can come more frequently!< /review><date>1550429551661<//date></record></dataset><record>

<review>The coveted 5 star! Any place that can make something called "Death Taco" actually taste bomb, deserves a high rating.  My sis had seen this place on social media a lot as of late, and seeing as how we are from the area, we decided to give it a whirl.

The Death Taco challenge is pretty simple, 1 super spicy taco eaten to completion, 10 minutes with no beverage. Surprisingly this taco really did taste great. If Genki cut out the spice, this is definitely a taco I would eat
regularly.  The spice on this thing set on pretty quick, but fizzled out after about 5 minutes. The girl behind the counter said that me and my sis handled it as good as anybody she has ever seen. Well now you reading this may seem optimistic by this point. We had won the challenge easily. By ten minutes, the spice was completely gone. This is where things took a turn for the worse. At around fifteen minutes both of our stomachs
were in knots. I went to the restroom and threw up. When I came out my sis was gone and she was a few doors down eating ice cream. Well death came-a-knockin on her door next. Since shes a lady, I wont get into details. All in all our stomachs were in major pain for about 4 hours.

Anybody can tap out of the mouth spice, but there is no tapping out of stomach pain. Tread with caution.

While we were there, we had plenty of time to see the other food coming out of the kitchen and it all seemed amazing. I will definitely be coming back to try it all!

Until next time...< /review><user_id>103960026898958587973< /user_id>< resp>

<Resp>None<//Resp><user>103960026898958587973< /user><user_name>michael e</user_name><Rating>5</Rating><gmapID>0x80dcafcbff4ba12f:0x80fa65d7d95af2b3< /gmapID>< review>
The coveted 5 star! Any place that can make something called "Death Taco" actually taste bomb, deserves a high rating.  My sis had seen this place on social media a lot as of late, and seeing as how we are from the area, we decided to give it a whirl.

The Death Taco challenge is pretty simple, 1 super spicy taco eaten to completion, 10 minutes with no beverage. Surprisingly this taco really did taste great. If Genki cut out the spice, this is definitely a taco I would eat
regularly.  The spice on this thing set on pretty quick, but fizzled out after about 5 minutes. The girl behind the counter said that me and my sis handled it as good as anybody she has ever seen. Well now you reading this may seem optimistic by this point. We had won the challenge easily. By ten minutes, the spice was completely gone. This is where things took a turn for the worse. At around fifteen minutes both of our stomachs
were in knots. I went to the restroom and threw up. When I came out my sis was gone and she was a few doors down eating ice cream. Well death came-a-knockin on her door next. Since shes a lady, I wont get into details. All in all our stomachs were in major pain for about 4 hours.

Anybody can tap out of the mouth spice, but there is no tapping out of stomach pain. Tread with caution.

While we were there, we had plenty of time to see the other food coming out of the kitchen and it all seemed amazing. I will definitely be coming back to try it all!

Until next time...< /review>

<username>Keith Miyake< /username><Date>1529359651868< /Date>< Rating>
2< /Rating>
< Review>
Had an order of beef ninja fries, a furious chicken, and cali burrito. Calling the food mediocre is a stretch. The "ninja" sauce tries to sneak attack your taste buds by overloading them with sugar and salt to mask the lack of nuance. It is way too sweet and tastes like bad teriyaki sauce mixed with bad sweet and sour sauce. The meats were overcooked and dry. The fries limp. The rice dry and stale tasting.

The burrito was also pretty gross. It's like a garbage burrito where they just stuff as much random ass stuff in it to hide the fact that nothing individually has good flavor.

The fries were limp and overly seasoned with Lawry's salt, which is totally unnecessary since they're smothered in nacho cheese and salty meat, and topped with way too much of their "ninja" sauce.

Also, I asked for 3 "drops" of their death sauce when they asked, but the server insisted on only 2. It was not spicy at all. Next time the customer is a jerk and insists on 3 drops, just give it to them and let them suffer the consequences of their stubbornness, or in this case, insistence that they could handle it.

Oh, and the inside of the restaurant smelled like a casino full of stale cigarette smoke. Yummmmmy.<//Review>

< review>
Active Duty military stay away until they get their billing practices in order. Dr. Sheikh is a good dentist and the staff are genuinely caring but the billing practices and office manager require a warning to potential customers.

Summary: Dentist is trying to recoup claims from patients after the insurance company denied for failure to submit within 12 months of service. Per their contract with MetLife they are not allowed to do this. When challenged regarding the validity of the bill the office waives this particular charge and magically finds others in my account from 2 years ago which had never been mentioned....Reported to the MetLife fraud department. Contact your insurance company before paying them any new charges on old services.

Details:
My dependents were patients in this clinic until we PCS'd summer of 2015. In January of 2017 we received a bill for services rendered in Feb/March of 2015 (nearly 2 years after the date of service).

I found this a bit odd so I decided to call and request an explanation for the late invoice. I was told by Discovery Children's Dentistry that they had sent the bill to MetLife on multiple occasions but the claim had been rejected. Discovery Children's Dentistry proceeds to tell me I am still responsible and sometimes this happens on occasion. Upon request they sent a detailed invoice and history of our family account. This claim was stated as the only outstanding charge.

I decided to call MetLife because something did not sound right. After giving MetLife the usual information to confirm my identity they are able to pull up the exact claim Discovery Children's Dentistry is referring to and admit that they denied the claim because the dentist failed to file the claim within the allotted window (12 months). I was then told that under the contract signed between the dentist and the insurance company if the claim does not reach MetLife within 12 months after the date of service they are allowed to deny reimbursement. Also, if the dentist is denied reimbursement because of their negligence (timeliness) then they are not allowed to attempt to recoup cost from the patient. MetLife said if the dentist had an issue they were more than welcome to call and discuss the claim.

I sent this information to Discovery Children's Dentistry via email requesting acknowledgement of receipt and a request that they void all charges. No Reply.

I then called Discovery Children's dentistry back and relayed the information provided by MetLife. The dentist said they would waive the debt for "professional courtesy" but denied lying about submitting it on multiple occasion's within the required time frame.

I thought it was finished.....

I then received a written statement in the mail that documented the removal of the erroneous charges but contained additional charges for services performed on another dependent within the same time period.

The dentist removed one set of charges because they had to (in accordance with the contract they signed) but then added charges for another dependent nearly two years after we leave the state.....when does it end?

If you receive a bill that seems strange get an itemized list from Discovery Children's Dentistry and call your insurance provider before  paying the charge. It may not be what it seems.< /review>

<Review>The employees at the Public Storage on Raytheon Road in San Diego, California are either in need of retraining or should learn how to leave personal problems out of the workplace. I am in town for my wedding and decided to check up on the two storage units i rent at this location. My first visit was on Tuesday August 23rd. I showed up at the location at 5:25 p.m. to inquire about cutting the locks on my units, as the keys had been misplaced in the four years since I acquired the units. The office was closed (?) and a sign stated that the manager would be back at 5:30 p.m. so, I decided to wait. At 5:54 p.m., an employee arrived and unlocked the doors to assist the 3 customers who had been waiting along with me. Although I was slightly irritated, the gentleman was helpful. He informed me that the manager was the person who performed the lock cutting at no charge, but that the manager wouldn't be there until the next day. He took my name, number, and unit numbers and told me that the manager would contact me the next day. He told me that an alternative to get it done the same day would be to hire a locksmith. I opted to have the manager contact me as I wasn't in a huge hurry and would prefer to speak to him, should I have any questions or concerns about my units. The next day (August 24th), I hadn't heard from the manager so, I stopped by again between 12 p.m. and 12:30 p.m. The middle aged employee in the office informed me that she had received the note from the previous employee that I needed the locks cut. She told me that I hadn't been contacted because the manager hadn't come in and wouldn't be in until Friday, when I am set to fly back home. I reiterated to her that I was told the manager would be in, today, and that's why I came back, instead of hiring the locksmith the previous day and she proceeded to tell me that the manager has "many responsibilities and cutting locks is not one of them. If I had been given the correct information at the beginning, i wouldn't had to have come and interrupt her busy day in the empty office. The office being closed during business hours, managers not showing up, and a lack of customer service skills is not good business. I'm sure Public Storage makes plenty of money, I just believe that apt employees would make more money for the company. < Text>
Having moved from Australia recently, I'm always on the look out for a good flat white. I had some friends in town yesterday and we stumbled upon Tiago just per chance as we were in the area.

I got the flat white, and I have to say its the best flat white I have had since being here in the USA. The young female barista knew exactly what she was doing, and it was re-assuring that she didn't ask if I meant "The drink they sell at Starbucks". It came in a 5.5 oz cup, consistency of the milk was dead on what I would expect (its not a no foam latte!). The roast tasted a little darker than some of the more independent coffee places i've been to, which I actually prefer. I'll definitely be making my way back there again!</Text>
